In 2019, at least 55 elephants died because of the drought.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> Severe storms are rare.<sup id="cite_ref-Baughan,_M._2005_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Baughan,_M._2005-111">[111]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">Biodiversity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Zimbabwe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Biodiversity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Zimbabwe" title="Wildlife of Zimbabwe">Wildlife of Zimbabwe</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Curled_trunk.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Curled_trunk.jpg/220px-Curled_trunk.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Curled_trunk.jpg/330px-Curled_trunk.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Curled_trunk.jpg/440px-Curled_trunk.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1167" data-file-height="787"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Curled_trunk.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>An elephant at a water hole in <a href="/wiki/Hwange_National_Park" title="Hwange National Park">Hwange National Park</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Zimbabwe contains seven terrestrial ecoregions: <a href="/wiki/Kalahari_Acacia-Baikiaea_woodlands" class="mw-redirect" title="Kalahari Acacia-Baikiaea woodlands">Kalahari Acacia-Baikiaea woodlands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southern_Africa_bushveld" class="mw-redirect" title="Southern Africa bushveld">Southern Africa bushveld</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southern_miombo_woodlands" title="Southern miombo woodlands">Southern miombo woodlands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zambezian_Baikiaea_woodlands" title="Zambezian Baikiaea woodlands">Zambezian Baikiaea woodlands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zambezian_and_mopane_woodlands" title="Zambezian and mopane woodlands">Zambezian and mopane woodlands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zambezian_halophytics" class="mw-redirect" title="Zambezian halophytics">Zambezian halophytics</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Zimbabwe_montane_forest-grassland_mosaic" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Zimbabwe montane forest-grassland mosaic">Eastern Zimbabwe montane forest-grassland mosaic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-112">[112]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The country is mostly savannah, although the moist and mountainous eastern highlands support areas of tropical evergreen and hardwood forests. Trees found in these Eastern Highlands include <a href="/wiki/Teak" title="Teak">teak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mahogany" title="Mahogany">mahogany</a>, enormous specimens of strangling fig, <a href="/wiki/Newtonia_buchananii" title="Newtonia buchananii">forest Newtonia</a>, big leaf, white stinkwood, chirinda stinkwood, knobthorn and many others. </p>
      <p>In the low-lying parts of the country fever trees, mopane, combretum and baobabs abound. Much of the country is covered by miombo woodland, dominated by brachystegia species and others. Among the numerous flowers and shrubs are hibiscus, flame lily, snake lily, spider lily, leonotus, cassia, tree wisteria and dombeya. There are around 350 species of mammals that can be found in Zimbabwe. There are also many snakes and lizards, over 500 bird species, and 131 fish species. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_issues">Environmental issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Zimbabwe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Environmental issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Large parts of Zimbabwe were once covered by forests with abundant wildlife. <a href="/wiki/Deforestation" title="Deforestation">Deforestation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Poaching" title="Poaching">poaching</a> has reduced the amount of wildlife. <a href="/wiki/Land_degradation" title="Land degradation">Woodland degradation</a> and deforestation, due to <a href="/wiki/Population_growth" title="Population growth">population growth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Urban_expansion" class="mw-redirect" title="Urban expansion">urban expansion</a> and lack of fuel, are major concerns<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> and have led to erosion and land degradation which diminish the amount of fertile soil. Local farmers have also been criticised by environmentalists for burning off vegetation to heat their tobacco barns.<sup id="cite_ref-Forestry_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forestry-114">[114]</a></sup> The country had a 2019 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 6.31/10, ranking it 81st globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-115">[115]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Zimbabwe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Government and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Zimbabwe" title="Politics of Zimbabwe">Politics of Zimbabwe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Zimbabwe" title="Elections in Zimbabwe">Elections in Zimbabwe</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Zimbabwe is a republic with a <a href="/wiki/Presidential_system" title="Presidential system">presidential system</a> of government. The <a href="/wiki/Semi-presidential_system" title="Semi-presidential system">semi-presidential system</a> was abolished with the adoption of a new constitution after a <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwean_constitutional_referendum,_2013" class="mw-redirect" title="Zimbabwean constitutional referendum, 2013">referendum</a> in March 2013. Under the constitutional changes in 2005, an <a href="/wiki/Upper_chamber" class="mw-redirect" title="Upper chamber">upper chamber</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Senate_of_Zimbabwe" title="Senate of Zimbabwe">Senate</a>, was reinstated.<sup id="cite_ref-reinstated_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reinstated-116">[116]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/House_of_Assembly_of_Zimbabwe" class="mw-redirect" title="House of Assembly of Zimbabwe">House of Assembly</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Lower_chamber" class="mw-redirect" title="Lower chamber">lower chamber</a> of Parliament. Former President <a href="/wiki/Robert_Mugabe" title="Robert Mugabe">Robert Mugabe</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe_African_National_Union_%E2%80%93_Patriotic_Front" class="mw-redirect" title="Zimbabwe African National Union – Patriotic Front">Zimbabwe African National Union – Patriotic Front</a> (commonly abbreviated ZANU–PF) has been the dominant political party in Zimbabwe since independence.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Harare_parlament_24032005.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Harare_parlament_24032005.jpg/220px-Harare_parlament_24032005.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="127" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Harare_parlament_24032005.jpg/330px-Harare_parlament_24032005.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Harare_parlament_24032005.jpg/440px-Harare_parlament_24032005.jpg 2x" data-file-width="674" data-file-height="390"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Harare_parlament_24032005.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Zimbabwe" title="Parliament of Zimbabwe">Parliament of Zimbabwe</a> in Harare
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In 1987 then-prime minister Mugabe revised the constitution, abolishing the <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_republic" title="Parliamentary republic">ceremonial presidency</a> and the prime ministerial posts to form an executive president, a <a href="/wiki/Presidential_system" title="Presidential system">Presidential system</a>. His ZANU party has won every election since independence, in the 1990 election the second-placed party, <a href="/wiki/Edgar_Tekere" title="Edgar Tekere">Edgar Tekere</a>'s Zimbabwe Unity Movement, obtained 20% of the vote.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>During the 1995 parliamentary elections most opposition parties, including the ZUM, boycotted the voting, resulting in a near-sweep by the ruling party.<sup id="cite_ref-Frankel_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frankel-119">[119]</a></sup> When the opposition returned to the polls in 2000, they won 57 seats, only five fewer than ZANU.<sup id="cite_ref-Frankel_119-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frankel-119">[119]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/2002_Zimbabwean_presidential_election" title="2002 Zimbabwean presidential election">Presidential elections were again held in 2002</a> amid allegations of vote-rigging, intimidation and fraud.<sup id="cite_ref-allegations_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allegations-120">[120]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe_parliamentary_elections,_2005" class="mw-redirect" title="Zimbabwe parliamentary elections, 2005">2005 Zimbabwe parliamentary elections</a> were held on 31 March and multiple claims of vote rigging, election fraud and intimidation were made by the MDC and <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Moyo" title="Jonathan Moyo">Jonathan Moyo</a>, calling for investigations into 32 of the 120 constituencies.<sup id="cite_ref-moyo_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-moyo-121">[121]</a></sup> Jonathan Moyo participated in the elections despite the allegations and won a seat as an independent member of Parliament.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>General elections were again held in Zimbabwe on 30 March 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> The official results required a run-off between Mugabe and <a href="/wiki/Morgan_Tsvangirai" title="Morgan Tsvangirai">Morgan Tsvangirai</a>, the opposition leader; the MDC challenged these results, claiming widespread election fraud by the Mugabe government.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The run-off was scheduled for 27 June 2008. On 22 June, citing the continuing unfairness of the process and refusing to participate in a "violent, illegitimate sham of an election process", Tsvangirai pulled out of the presidential run-off, the ZEC held the run-off and President Mugabe received a landslide majority.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Election_campaign_March_2005.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Election_campaign_March_2005.jpg/220px-Election_campaign_March_2005.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Election_campaign_March_2005.jpg/330px-Election_campaign_March_2005.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Election_campaign_March_2005.jpg/440px-Election_campaign_March_2005.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2240" data-file-height="1488"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Election_campaign_March_2005.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Supporters of the <a href="/wiki/Movement_for_Democratic_Change_(prior_to_2005)" class="mw-redirect" title="Movement for Democratic Change (prior to 2005)">Movement for Democratic Change</a> in 2005.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/MDC-T" class="mw-redirect" title="MDC-T">MDC-T</a> led by Morgan Tsvangirai is now the majority in the Lower chamber of Parliament. The MDC split into two factions. One faction (<a href="/wiki/MDC-M" class="mw-redirect" title="MDC-M">MDC-M</a>), now led by <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Mutambara" title="Arthur Mutambara">Arthur Mutambara</a> contested the elections to the Senate, while the other, led by Tsvangirai, opposed to contesting the elections, stating that participation in a rigged election is tantamount to endorsing Mugabe's claim that past elections were free and fair. The opposition parties have resumed participation in national and local elections as recently as 2006. The two MDC camps had their congresses in 2006 with Tsvangirai being elected to lead <a href="/wiki/MDC-T" class="mw-redirect" title="MDC-T">MDC-T</a>, which has become more popular than the other group.<sup id="cite_ref-findarticles1_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-findarticles1-125">[125]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Mutambara, a robotics professor and former <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> robotics specialist has replaced <a href="/wiki/Welshman_Ncube" title="Welshman Ncube">Welshman Ncube</a> who was the interim leader of MDC-M after the split. Morgan Tsvangirai did not participate in the Senate elections, while the Mutambara faction participated and won five seats in the Senate. The Mutambara formation has been weakened by defections from MPs and individuals who are disillusioned by their manifesto. As of 2008<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Zimbabwe&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the Movement for Democratic Change has become the most popular, with crowds as large as 20,000 attending their rallies as compared to between 500 and 5,000 for the other formation.<sup id="cite_ref-findarticles1_125-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-findarticles1-125">[125]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 28 April 2008, Tsvangirai and Mutambara announced at a joint news conference in <a href="/wiki/Johannesburg" title="Johannesburg">Johannesburg</a> that the two MDC formations were co-operating, enabling the MDC to have a clear parliamentary majority.<sup id="cite_ref-SABCre_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SABCre-126">[126]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Reunites_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reunites-127">[127]</a></sup> Tsvangirai said that Mugabe could not remain President without a parliamentary majority.<sup id="cite_ref-Reunites_127-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reunites-127">[127]</a></sup> On the same day, Silaigwana announced that the recounts for the final five constituencies had been completed, that the results were being collated and that they would be published on 29 April.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In mid-September 2008, after protracted negotiations overseen by the leaders of South Africa and Mozambique, Mugabe and Tsvangirai signed a power-sharing deal which would see Mugabe retain control over the army. Donor nations have adopted a 'wait-and-see' attitude, wanting to see real change being brought about by this merger before committing themselves to funding rebuilding efforts, which are estimated to take at least five years. On 11 February 2009 Tsvangirai was sworn in as Prime Minister by President Mugabe.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In November 2008, the government of Zimbabwe spent US$7.3 million donated by the <a href="/wiki/Global_Fund_to_Fight_AIDS,_Tuberculosis_and_Malaria" class="mw-redirect" title="Global Fund to Fight AIDS, Tuberculosis and Malaria">Global Fund to Fight AIDS, Tuberculosis and Malaria</a>. A representative of the organisation declined to speculate on how the money was spent, except that it was not for the intended purpose, and the government has failed to honour requests to return the money.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In February 2013, Zimbabwe's election chief, <a href="/wiki/Simpson_Mtambanengwe" class="mw-redirect" title="Simpson Mtambanengwe">Simpson Mtambanengwe</a>, resigned due to ill health. His resignation came months before the country's constitutional referendum and elections.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Status of Zimbabwe politics has been thrown into question by a coup taking place in November 2017, ending Mugabe's 30 year presidential incumbency. <a href="/wiki/Emmerson_Mnangagwa" title="Emmerson Mnangagwa">Emmerson Mnangagwa</a> was appointed president following this coup, and officially elected with 50.8% of the vote in the <a href="/wiki/2018_Zimbabwean_general_election" title="2018 Zimbabwean general election">2018 Zimbabwean general election</a>, avoiding a run-off and making him the 3rd President of Zimbabwe. </p>
      <p>The government has received negative comments among its citizen for always shutting down the internet in the past amid protests such as the one planned on the 31st of July. 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Zimbabwe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Zimbabwe" title="Foreign relations of Zimbabwe">Foreign relations of Zimbabwe</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Zimbabwe maintains relations with various countries around the world, and maintains close diplomatic relations with neighboring nations. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Armed_forces">Armed forces</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Zimbabwe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Armed forces">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399"></a>

          <div class="mbox-text-span">

      </table> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe_Defence_Forces" title="Zimbabwe Defence Forces">Zimbabwe Defence Forces</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_Zimbabwe_Defence_Forces.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Flag_of_the_Zimbabwe_Defence_Forces.svg/220px-Flag_of_the_Zimbabwe_Defence_Forces.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Flag_of_the_Zimbabwe_Defence_Forces.svg/330px-Flag_of_the_Zimbabwe_Defence_Forces.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Flag_of_the_Zimbabwe_Defence_Forces.svg/440px-Flag_of_the_Zimbabwe_Defence_Forces.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="950" data-file-height="587"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_Zimbabwe_Defence_Forces.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The flag of the <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe_Defence_Forces" title="Zimbabwe Defence Forces">Zimbabwe Defence Forces</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Zimbabwe Defence Forces were set up by unifying three insurrectionist forces – the <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe_African_National_Liberation_Army" title="Zimbabwe African National Liberation Army">Zimbabwe African National Liberation Army</a> (ZANLA), the <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe_People%27s_Revolutionary_Army" title="Zimbabwe People's Revolutionary Army">Zimbabwe People's Revolutionary Army</a> (ZIPRA), and the <a href="/wiki/Rhodesian_Security_Forces" title="Rhodesian Security Forces">Rhodesian Security Forces</a> (RSF) – after the <a href="/wiki/Second_Chimurenga" class="mw-redirect" title="Second Chimurenga">Second Chimurenga</a> and Zimbabwean independence in 1980. The integration period saw the formation of the <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe_National_Army" title="Zimbabwe National Army">Zimbabwe National Army</a> (ZNA) and <a href="/wiki/Air_Force_of_Zimbabwe" title="Air Force of Zimbabwe">Air Force of Zimbabwe</a> (AFZ) as separate entities under the command of Rtd General <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Mujuru" title="Solomon Mujuru">Solomon Mujuru</a> and Air Marshal <a href="/wiki/Norman_Walsh" title="Norman Walsh">Norman Walsh</a> who retired in 1982, and was replaced by Air Marshal Azim Daudpota who handed over command to Rtd <a href="/wiki/Air_Chief_Marshal" class="mw-redirect" title="Air Chief Marshal">Air Chief Marshal</a> <a href="/wiki/Josiah_Tungamirai" title="Josiah Tungamirai">Josiah Tungamirai</a> in 1985. </p>
      <p>In December 2003, General Constantine Chiwenga, was promoted and appointed Commander of the Zimbabwe Defence Forces. Lieutenant General P. V. Sibanda replaced him as Commander of the Army.<sup id="cite_ref-minist_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-minist-134">[134]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The ZNA has an active duty strength of 30,000. The Air Force has about 5,139 standing personnel.<sup id="cite_ref-Airforce_of_Zimbabwe_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Airforce_of_Zimbabwe-135">[135]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe_Republic_Police" title="Zimbabwe Republic Police">Zimbabwe Republic Police</a> (includes Police Support Unit, Paramilitary Police) is part of the Zimbabwe Defence Forces and numbers 25,000.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Following majority rule in early 1980, <a href="/wiki/British_Army" title="British Army">British Army</a> trainers oversaw the integration of guerrilla fighters into a <a href="/wiki/Battalion" title="Battalion">battalion</a> structure overlaid on the existing Rhodesian armed forces. For the first year, a system was followed where the top-performing candidate became battalion commander. If he or she was from ZANLA, then his or her second-in-command was the top-performing ZIPRA candidate, and vice versa.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> This ensured a balance between the two movements in the command structure. From early 1981, this system was abandoned in favour of political appointments, and ZANLA and ZANU fighters consequently quickly formed the majority of battalion commanders in the ZNA.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>The ZNA was originally formed into four <a href="/wiki/Brigade" title="Brigade">brigades</a>, composed of a total of 28 battalions. The brigade support units were composed almost entirely of specialists of the former Rhodesian Army, while unintegrated battalions of the <a href="/wiki/Rhodesian_African_Rifles" title="Rhodesian African Rifles">Rhodesian African Rifles</a> were assigned to the 1st, 3rd and 4th Brigades. The <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwean_Fifth_Brigade" class="mw-redirect" title="Zimbabwean Fifth Brigade">Fifth Brigade</a> was formed in 1981 and disbanded in 1988 after the demonstration of mass brutality and murder during the brigade's occupation of <a href="/wiki/Matabeleland" title="Matabeleland">Matabeleland</a> in what has become known as <a href="/wiki/Gukurahundi" title="Gukurahundi">Gukurahundi</a> (<a href="/wiki/Shona_language" title="Shona language">Shona</a>: <i lang="sn">"the early rain which washes away the chaff before the spring rains"</i>), the campaign which finished off Mugabe's liberation struggle.<sup id="cite_ref-watch_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-watch-53">[53]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> The Brigade had been re-formed by 2006, with its commander, Brigadier-General John Mupande praising its "rich history".<sup id="cite_ref-Herald_Reporter_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Herald_Reporter-139">[139]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Zimbabwe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Zimbabwe" title="Human rights in Zimbabwe">Human rights in Zimbabwe</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Child_marriage_in_Zimbabwe" title="Child marriage in Zimbabwe">Child marriage in Zimbabwe</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Demonstration_against_Mugabe.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Demonstration_against_Mugabe.JPG/220px-Demonstration_against_Mugabe.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Demonstration_against_Mugabe.JPG/330px-Demonstration_against_Mugabe.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Demonstration_against_Mugabe.JPG/440px-Demonstration_against_Mugabe.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1952"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Demonstration_against_Mugabe.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A demonstration in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> against <a href="/wiki/Robert_Mugabe" title="Robert Mugabe">Robert Mugabe</a>. Protests are discouraged by Zimbabwean police in Zimbabwe.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>There are widespread reports of systematic and escalating violations of human rights in Zimbabwe under the <a href="/wiki/Robert_Mugabe" title="Robert Mugabe">Mugabe administration</a> and the dominant party, the <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe_African_National_Union_-_Patriotic_Front" class="mw-redirect" title="Zimbabwe African National Union - Patriotic Front">ZANU–PF</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to human rights organisations such as <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a><sup id="cite_ref-AI_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AI-142">[142]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a><sup id="cite_ref-hrw_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrw-143">[143]</a></sup> the government of Zimbabwe violates the rights to shelter, food, <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_movement" title="Freedom of movement">freedom of movement</a> and residence, <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_assembly" title="Freedom of assembly">freedom of assembly</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Rule_of_law" title="Rule of law">protection of the law</a>. In 2009, Gregory Stanton, then President of the International Association of Genocide Scholars, stated there was "clear evidence that Mugabe government was guilty of crimes against humanity and that there was sufficient evidence of crimes against humanity to bring Mugabe to trial in front of the International Criminal Court.”<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Male <a href="/wiki/Homosexuality" title="Homosexuality">homosexuality</a> is <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Zimbabwe" title="LGBT rights in Zimbabwe">illegal in Zimbabwe</a>. Since 1995, the government has <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_opposition" title="LGBT rights opposition">carried out campaigns</a> against both homosexual men and women.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> President Mugabe has blamed gays for many of Zimbabwe's problems and viewed homosexuality as an "un-African" and immoral culture brought by European colonists and practised by only "a few whites" in his country.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Opposition gatherings are frequently the subject of reprisals by the police force, such as the crackdown on an 11 March 2007 <a href="/wiki/Movement_for_Democratic_Change_%E2%80%93_Tsvangirai" title="Movement for Democratic Change – Tsvangirai">Movement for Democratic Change</a> (MDC) rally and several others during the 2008 election campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> Police actions have been strongly condemned by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Secretary-General" class="mw-redirect" title="United Nations Secretary-General">UN Secretary-General</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ban_Ki-moon" title="Ban Ki-moon">Ban Ki-moon</a>, the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> and the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_Morgan_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc_Morgan-148">[148]</a></sup> While noting that the activists had suffered injuries, but not mentioning the cause of them,<sup id="cite_ref-herald_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-herald-149">[149]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There are also concerns over Fox Southwest media rights and access. The Zimbabwean government is accused of suppressing freedom of the press and freedom of speech.<sup id="cite_ref-AI_142-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AI-142">[142]</a></sup> It has been repeatedly accused of using the public broadcaster, the <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe_Broadcasting_Corporation" title="Zimbabwe Broadcasting Corporation">Zimbabwe Broadcasting Corporation</a>, as a propaganda tool.<sup id="cite_ref-propaganda_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-propaganda-150">[150]</a></sup> Newspapers critical of the government, such as the <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_News_(Harare)" title="Daily News (Harare)">Daily News</a></i>, closed after bombs exploded at their offices and the government refused to renew their licence.<sup id="cite_ref-bombs_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bombs-151">[151]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-license_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-license-152">[152]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/BBC_News" title="BBC News">BBC News</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sky_News" title="Sky News">Sky News</a>, and <a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">CNN</a> were banned from filming or reporting from Zimbabwe. In 2009 reporting restrictions on the BBC and CNN were lifted.<sup id="cite_ref-Telegraph_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Telegraph-153">[153]</a></sup> Sky News continue to report on happenings within Zimbabwe from neighbouring countries like South Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-networks_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-networks-154">[154]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 24 July 2020, the <a href="/wiki/Office_of_the_United_Nations_High_Commissioner_for_Human_Rights" title="Office of the United Nations High Commissioner for Human Rights">Office of the United Nations High Commissioner for Human Rights</a> (OHCHR) expressed concerns over allegations suggesting that Zimbabwean authorities may have used the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19</a> crisis as a pretext to suppress <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_speech" title="Freedom of speech">freedom of expression</a> and peaceful assembly on the streets. The OHCHR spokesperson, Liz Throssell stated that people have a right to protest corruption or anything else. The authorities in Zimbabwe used force to disperse and arrest nurses and health workers, who were peacefully protesting for better salaries and work conditions. The reports suggest that a few members of opposition party and investigative journalists were also arbitrarily arrested and detained for taking part in a protest.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On August 5, 2020, the #ZimbabweanLivesMatter campaign on <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a> drew attention of international celebrities and politicians towards <a href="/wiki/Human_rights" title="Human rights">human rights</a> abuses in the country, mounting pressure on <a href="/wiki/Emmerson_Mnangagwa" title="Emmerson Mnangagwa">Emmerson Mnangagwa</a>’s government. The campaign was in response to <a href="/wiki/Arrests" class="mw-redirect" title="Arrests">arrests</a>, abductions and <a href="/wiki/Torture" title="Torture">torture</a> of political activists and the incarceration of the journalist, <a href="/wiki/Hopewell_Chin%27ono" title="Hopewell Chin'ono">Hopewell Chin'ono</a>, and the Booker prize long-listed author, <a href="/wiki/Tsitsi_Dangarembga" title="Tsitsi Dangarembga">Tsitsi Dangarembga</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Zimbabwe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Zimbabwe" title="Provinces of Zimbabwe">Provinces of Zimbabwe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Zimbabwe" title="Districts of Zimbabwe">Districts of Zimbabwe</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wards_of_Zimbabwe" class="mw-redirect" title="Wards of Zimbabwe">Wards of Zimbabwe</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Administrative_Divisions_of_Zimbabwe.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Administrative_Divisions_of_Zimbabwe.svg/300px-Administrative_Divisions_of_Zimbabwe.svg.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="233" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Administrative_Divisions_of_Zimbabwe.svg/450px-Administrative_Divisions_of_Zimbabwe.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Administrative_Divisions_of_Zimbabwe.svg/600px-Administrative_Divisions_of_Zimbabwe.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="630" data-file-height="490"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Administrative_Divisions_of_Zimbabwe.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Zimbabwe" title="Provinces of Zimbabwe">Administrative divisions of Zimbabwe</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Zimbabwe has a <a href="/wiki/Centralised_government" class="mw-redirect" title="Centralised government">centralised government</a> and is divided into eight provinces and two cities with provincial status, for administrative purposes. Each province has a provincial capital from where government administration is usually carried out.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA-WF_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-WF-2">[2]</a></sup> </p> 
      <table class="wikitable" style="text-align:center;"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>

         <td><a href="/wiki/Mashonaland_Central" class="mw-redirect" title="Mashonaland Central">Mashonaland Central</a></td>

         <td><a href="/wiki/Gweru" title="Gweru">Gweru</a> </td>

       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>The names of most of the provinces were generated from the <a href="/wiki/Mashonaland" title="Mashonaland">Mashonaland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Matabeleland" title="Matabeleland">Matabeleland</a> divide at the time of colonisation: Mashonaland was the territory occupied first by the British South Africa Company Pioneer Column and Matabeleland the territory conquered during the <a href="/wiki/First_Matabele_War" title="First Matabele War">First Matabele War</a>. This corresponds roughly to the precolonial territory of the <a href="/wiki/Shona_people" title="Shona people">Shona people</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Matabele_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Matabele people">Matabele people</a>, although there are significant ethnic minorities in most provinces. Each province is headed by a Provincial Governor, appointed by the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Zimbabwe" title="President of Zimbabwe">President</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-constitution_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-constitution-158">[158]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The provincial government is run by a Provincial Administrator, appointed by the Public Service Commission. Other government functions at provincial level are carried out by provincial offices of national government departments.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The provinces are subdivided into 59 <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Zimbabwe" title="Districts of Zimbabwe">districts</a> and 1,200 <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Zimbabwe" class="mw-redirect" title="Municipalities of Zimbabwe">wards</a> (sometimes referred to as municipalities). Each district is headed by a District Administrator, appointed by the Public Service Commission. There is also a Rural District Council, which appoints a chief executive officer. The Rural District Council is composed of elected ward councillors, the District Administrator and one representative of the chiefs (traditional leaders appointed under customary law) in the district. Other government functions at district level are carried out by district offices of national government departments.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>At the ward level there is a Ward Development Committee, comprising the elected ward councillor, the kraalheads (traditional leaders subordinate to chiefs) and representatives of Village Development Committees. Wards are subdivided into villages, each of which has an elected Village Development Committee and a Headman (traditional leader subordinate to the kraalhead).<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Zimbabwe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Zimbabwe" title="Economy of Zimbabwe">Economy of Zimbabwe</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_zwe_all_show_2010_SITC4.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Tree_map_export_zwe_all_show_2010_SITC4.svg/330px-Tree_map_export_zwe_all_show_2010_SITC4.svg.png" decoding="async" width="330" height="330" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Tree_map_export_zwe_all_show_2010_SITC4.svg/495px-Tree_map_export_zwe_all_show_2010_SITC4.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Tree_map_export_zwe_all_show_2010_SITC4.svg/660px-Tree_map_export_zwe_all_show_2010_SITC4.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="512"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_zwe_all_show_2010_SITC4.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A proportional representation of Zimbabwe's exports, 2010
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Minerals, gold,<sup id="cite_ref-Baughan,_M._2005_111-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Baughan,_M._2005-111">[111]</a></sup> and agriculture are the main foreign exports of Zimbabwe. Tourism also plays a key role in its economy.<sup id="cite_ref-FA_Canada_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FA_Canada-162">[162]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The mining sector remains very lucrative, with some of the world's largest <a href="/wiki/Platinum" title="Platinum">platinum</a> reserves being mined by <a href="/wiki/Anglo_American_plc" title="Anglo American plc">Anglo American plc</a> and Impala Platinum.<sup id="cite_ref-nofix_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nofix-163">[163]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Marange_diamond_fields" title="Marange diamond fields">Marange diamond fields</a>, discovered in 2006, are considered the biggest diamond find in over a century.<sup id="cite_ref-EarthTimes_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EarthTimes-164">[164]</a></sup> They have the potential to improve the fiscal situation of the country considerably, but almost all revenues from the field have disappeared into the pockets of army officers and ZANU–PF politicians.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In terms of carats produced, the Marange field is one of the largest diamond producing projects in the world,<sup id="cite_ref-Kitco_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kitco-166">[166]</a></sup> estimated to produce 12 million carats in 2014 worth over $350 million.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> Zimbabwe is the biggest trading partner of South Africa on the continent.<sup id="cite_ref-AN_economy_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AN_economy-168">[168]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Taxes and tariffs are high for private enterprises, while state enterprises are strongly subsidised. State regulation is costly to companies; starting or closing a business is slow and costly.<sup id="cite_ref-Heritage:_Zimbabwe_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heritage:_Zimbabwe-169">[169]</a></sup> Government spending was predicted to reach 67% of GDP in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Tourism was an important industry for the country, but has been failing in recent years. The Zimbabwe Conservation Task Force released a report in June 2007, estimating 60% of Zimbabwe's wildlife has died since 2000 due to poaching and deforestation. The report warns that the loss of life combined with widespread <a href="/wiki/Deforestation" title="Deforestation">deforestation</a> is potentially disastrous for the tourist industry.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Information_and_communications_technology" title="Information and communications technology">ICT</a> sector of Zimbabwe has been growing at a fast pace. A report by the mobile internet browser company, Opera, in June/July 2011 has ranked Zimbabwe as Africa's fastest growing market.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:2010_market_Harare_Zimbabwe_5866074969.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/2010_market_Harare_Zimbabwe_5866074969.jpg/220px-2010_market_Harare_Zimbabwe_5866074969.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/2010_market_Harare_Zimbabwe_5866074969.jpg/330px-2010_market_Harare_Zimbabwe_5866074969.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/2010_market_Harare_Zimbabwe_5866074969.jpg/440px-2010_market_Harare_Zimbabwe_5866074969.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1824" data-file-height="1368"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:2010_market_Harare_Zimbabwe_5866074969.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A market in <a href="/wiki/Mbare,_Harare" title="Mbare, Harare">Mbare, Harare</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Since 1 January 2002, the government of Zimbabwe has had its lines of credit at international financial institutions frozen, through US legislation called the <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe_Democracy_and_Economic_Recovery_Act_of_2001" title="Zimbabwe Democracy and Economic Recovery Act of 2001">Zimbabwe Democracy and Economic Recovery Act of 2001</a> (ZDERA). Section 4C instructs the Secretary of the Treasury to direct directors at international financial institutions to veto the extension of loans and credit to the Zimbabwean government.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup> According to the United States, these <a href="/wiki/Economic_sanctions" title="Economic sanctions">sanctions</a> target only seven specific businesses owned or controlled by government officials and not ordinary citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:GDP_per_capita_(current),_%25_of_world_average,_1960-2012;_Zimbabwe,_South_Africa,_Botswana,_Zambia,_Mozambique.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/GDP_per_capita_%28current%29%2C_%25_of_world_average%2C_1960-2012%3B_Zimbabwe%2C_South_Africa%2C_Botswana%2C_Zambia%2C_Mozambique.png/350px-GDP_per_capita_%28current%29%2C_%25_of_world_average%2C_1960-2012%3B_Zimbabwe%2C_South_Africa%2C_Botswana%2C_Zambia%2C_Mozambique.png" decoding="async" width="350" height="232" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/GDP_per_capita_%28current%29%2C_%25_of_world_average%2C_1960-2012%3B_Zimbabwe%2C_South_Africa%2C_Botswana%2C_Zambia%2C_Mozambique.png/525px-GDP_per_capita_%28current%29%2C_%25_of_world_average%2C_1960-2012%3B_Zimbabwe%2C_South_Africa%2C_Botswana%2C_Zambia%2C_Mozambique.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/GDP_per_capita_%28current%29%2C_%25_of_world_average%2C_1960-2012%3B_Zimbabwe%2C_South_Africa%2C_Botswana%2C_Zambia%2C_Mozambique.png/700px-GDP_per_capita_%28current%29%2C_%25_of_world_average%2C_1960-2012%3B_Zimbabwe%2C_South_Africa%2C_Botswana%2C_Zambia%2C_Mozambique.png 2x" data-file-width="1055" data-file-height="700"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:GDP_per_capita_(current),_%25_of_world_average,_1960-2012;_Zimbabwe,_South_Africa,_Botswana,_Zambia,_Mozambique.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The GDP per capita (current), compared to neighbouring countries (world average = 100).
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Zimbabwe maintained positive economic growth throughout the 1980s (5% GDP growth per year) and 1990s (4.3% GDP growth per year). The economy declined from 2000: 5% decline in 2000, 8% in 2001, 12% in 2002 and 18% in 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup> Zimbabwe's involvement from 1998 to 2002 in the war in the Democratic Republic of the Congo drained hundreds of millions of dollars from the economy.<sup id="cite_ref-drained_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-drained-177">[177]</a></sup> From 1999 to 2009, Zimbabwe saw the lowest ever economic growth with an annual GDP decrease of 6.1%.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The downward spiral of the economy has been attributed mainly to mismanagement and corruption by the government and the eviction of more than 4,000 white farmers in the controversial land confiscations of 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-CNN-2000-04-18_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNN-2000-04-18-179">[179]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Time-2002-02-18_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Time-2002-02-18-180">[180]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-USAToday-2002-06-24_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USAToday-2002-06-24-181">[181]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBC-2002-08-15_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-2002-08-15-182">[182]</a></sup> The Zimbabwean government and its supporters attest that it was Western policies to avenge the expulsion of their kin that sabotaged the economy.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>By 2005, the purchasing power of the average Zimbabwean had dropped to the same levels in real terms as 1953.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup> In 2005, the government, led by central bank governor <a href="/wiki/Gideon_Gono" title="Gideon Gono">Gideon Gono</a>, started making overtures that white farmers could come back. There were 400 to 500 still left in the country, but much of the land that had been confiscated was no longer productive.<sup id="cite_ref-Meldrum-2005-05-21_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Meldrum-2005-05-21-185">[185]</a></sup> By 2016 there were about 300 farms owned by white farmers left out of the original 4,500. The farms left were either too remote or their owners had paid for protection or collaborated with the regime.<sup id="cite_ref-Out_of_House_89-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Out_of_House-89">[89]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In January 2007, the government issued long-term leases to some white farmers.<sup id="cite_ref-Timberg-WP-2007-01-06_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timberg-WP-2007-01-06-186">[186]</a></sup> At the same time, however, the government also continued to demand that all remaining white farmers, who were given eviction notices earlier, vacate the land or risk being arrested.<sup id="cite_ref-AP/WP-2007-02-05_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AP/WP-2007-02-05-187">[187]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Chinaka-2007-08-08_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chinaka-2007-08-08-188">[188]</a></sup> Mugabe pointed to foreign governments and alleged "sabotage" as the cause of the fall of the Zimbabwean economy, as well as the country's 80% formal unemployment rate.<sup id="cite_ref-unemployment_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unemployment-189">[189]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Inflation rose from an annual rate of 32% in 1998, to an official estimated high of 11,200,000% in August 2008 according to the country's Central Statistical Office.<sup id="cite_ref-Zimbabwe_inflation_at_11,200,000_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zimbabwe_inflation_at_11,200,000-190">[190]</a></sup> This represented a state of <a href="/wiki/Hyperinflation_in_Zimbabwe" title="Hyperinflation in Zimbabwe">hyperinflation</a>, and the central bank introduced a new 100 trillion dollar note.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 29 January 2009, in an effort to counteract runaway inflation, acting Finance Minister <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Chinamasa" title="Patrick Chinamasa">Patrick Chinamasa</a> announced that Zimbabweans will be permitted to use other, more stable currencies to do business, alongside the Zimbabwe dollar.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup> In an effort to combat inflation and foster economic growth the Zimbabwean dollar was suspended indefinitely on 12 April 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup> In 2016 Zimbabwe allowed trade in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">United States dollar</a> and various other currencies such as the <a href="/wiki/South_African_rand" title="South African rand">rand</a> (South Africa), the <a href="/wiki/Botswana_pula" title="Botswana pula">pula</a> (Botswana), the <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">euro</a>, and the Pound Sterling (UK).<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup> In February 2019, RBZ Governor introduced a new local currency, the <a href="/wiki/RTGS_Dollar" class="mw-redirect" title="RTGS Dollar">RTGS Dollar</a> in a move to address some of the Zimbabwean economic and financial challenges.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>After the formation of the Unity Government and the adoption of several currencies instead of the Zimbabwe dollar in 2009, the Zimbabwean economy rebounded. GDP grew by 8–9% a year between 2009 and 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-Worldbank_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Worldbank-196">[196]</a></sup> In November 2010, the IMF described the Zimbabwean economy as "completing its second year of buoyant economic growth".<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup> By 2014, Zimbabwe had recovered to levels seen in the 1990s<sup id="cite_ref-Worldbank_196-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Worldbank-196">[196]</a></sup> but between 2012 and 2016 growth faltered.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/w/index.php?title=Zimplats&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Zimplats (page does not exist)">Zimplats</a>, the nation's largest platinum company, has proceeded with US$500 million in expansions, and is also continuing a separate US$2 billion project, despite threats by Mugabe to nationalise the company.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup> The pan-African investment bank <a href="/w/index.php?title=IMARA_(bank)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="IMARA (bank) (page does not exist)">IMARA</a> released a favourable report in February 2011 on investment prospects in Zimbabwe, citing an improved revenue base and higher tax receipts.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In late January 2013, the Zimbabwean finance ministry reported that they had only $217 in their treasury and would apply for donations to finance the coming elections that is estimated to cost US$107 million.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As of October 2014, <a href="/wiki/Metallon_Corporation" title="Metallon Corporation">Metallon Corporation</a> was Zimbabwe's largest gold miner.<sup id="cite_ref-Metallon_203-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Metallon-203">[203]</a></sup> The group is looking to increase its production to 500,000 <a href="/wiki/Troy_weight" title="Troy weight">troy ounces</a> per annum by 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-Metallon_203-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Metallon-203">[203]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Inflation in Zimbabwe was 42% in 2018. In June 2019, the inflation rate reached 175%, leading to mass unrest across the country and in <a href="/wiki/Harare" title="Harare">Harare</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture">Agriculture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Zimbabwe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Agriculture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Zimbabwe's commercial farming sector was traditionally a source of exports and foreign exchange, and provided 400,000 jobs. However, the government's land reform program badly damaged the sector, turning Zimbabwe into a net importer of food products.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA-WF_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-WF-2">[2]</a></sup> For example, between 2000 and 2016, annual wheat production fell from 250,000 tons to 60,000 tons, maize was reduced from two million tons to 500,000 tons and cattle slaughtered for beef fell from 605,000 to 244,000.<sup id="cite_ref-Out_of_House_89-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Out_of_House-89">[89]</a></sup> Coffee production, once a prized export commodity, came to a virtual halt after seizure or expropriation of white-owned coffee farms in 2000 and has never recovered.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>For the past ten years, the <a href="/wiki/International_Crops_Research_Institute_for_the_Semi-Arid_Tropics" title="International Crops Research Institute for the Semi-Arid Tropics">International Crops Research Institute for the Semi-Arid Tropics</a> (<a href="/wiki/ICRISAT" class="mw-redirect" title="ICRISAT">ICRISAT</a>) has been assisting Zimbabwe's farmers to adopt <a href="/wiki/Conservation_agriculture" title="Conservation agriculture">conservation agriculture</a> techniques, a sustainable method of farming that can help increase yields. By applying the three principles of minimum soil disturbance, legume-based cropping and the use of organic mulch, farmers can improve infiltration, reduce evaporation and soil erosion, and build up organic soil content.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Between 2005 and 2011, the number of smallholders practising conservation agriculture in Zimbabwe increased from 5,000 to more than 150,000. Cereal yields rose between 15 and 100 per cent across different regions.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">[206]</a></sup> The government declared potato a national strategic food security crop on 18 May 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Mvurwi, a region in n Mashonaland Central Province, once fell in the "breadbasket region" of Zimbabwe, with fertile soils. However, over the past 30 years, this is one of the areas that have been negatively impacted by the land reforms, causing it to be less prosperous than it was in the late 20th century. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Zimbabwe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399"></a>
          </div></td>
         <td class="mbox-text">
          <div class="mbox-text-span">
